--- Commit Message ---
LU-5896 hsm: update data version if layout is changed

lfs hsm_archive file
lfs migrate -i1 tfile
lfs hsm_release file

This actions lead to "Cannot send HSM request ...
Device or resource busy" error. What happens because of
data version mismatch. The error originally returned by
the MDS is EPERM (in mdt_hsm_release()) but is translated
into EBUSY by ll_close_inode_openhandle().

Layout swap should check to see if the 'old' version matches the
archived version in the HSM xattr and update the HSM xattr.

migrate_nonblock() doesn't expect object version to be changed, so
no need sending objects versions to a server.

Change-Id: I80a352ce9f67ea3a694d792c51511e48570bde92
Signed-off-by: Artem Blagodarenko <artem.blagodarenko@hpe.com>

I am just realizing... This is a breaking change, right? If an older client were to send a swap layout request to a newer MDS, what would the `msl_dvs' field be initialized with on the server side?

Also, why isn't this caught in wiretest.c? (I can see there is no check for the mdc_swap_layout structure there).

What is the rule for a check to land in ptlrpc/wiretest.c?

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2019-12-03 01:21:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8: Code-Review-1

Could you please see the comments on https://jira.whamcloud.com/browse/LU-5896 and improve the patch accordingly?
Please note 
llapi_fswap_layouts_grouplock(fd, fdv, dv1, dv2, 0,
					   SWAP_LAYOUTS_CHECK_DV1 |
					   SWAP_LAYOUTS_CHECK_DV2);
This lapi interface is exposed to the user space, it may be  malicious used:
the content of file1 and file2 are not same, but the data are all synced to OSTs, thus both data_verion will not be changed. In this case, the archive data may be not incorrect after migration.

For safety, I think we need to move the data copy into kernel for file migration case.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-12-03 09:00:51.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

> Please note
 >
 > llapi_fswap_layouts_grouplock(fd, fdv, dv1, dv2, 0,
 >                               SWAP_LAYOUTS_CHECK_DV1 |
 >                               SWAP_LAYOUTS_CHECK_DV2);
 >
 > This lapi interface is exposed to the user space, it may be 
 > malicious used:
 > the content of file1 and file2 are not same, but the data are all
 > synced to OSTs, thus both data_verion will not be changed. In this
 > case, the archive data may be not incorrect after migration.
 > 
 > For safety, I think we need to move the data copy into kernel for
 > file migration case.

This has always been true for data migration, and is "safe enough" as long as the user has write permission on the file.  It is no more dangerous than a "malicious user" overwriting the file with any data that they want, because they already have write permission on the file.

--- Message (Artem Blagodarenko, 2019-12-03 09:34:38.000000000) ---

--- Message (Qian Yingjin, 2019-12-03 11:30:39.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

(2 comments)

When
swap_layouts o1 o2，
we must consider the following cases:
1. migrate
we know that the data content in o1 and o2 are same,
then it needs to indicate it via a flags SWAP_LAYOUTS_DATA_MIGRATE，
then when MDT know the swapping layouts is for data migration, it will do as following:

if o1 has been archived, check whether whether the archive is dirty (HS_DIRTY).
if so, do nothing to the HSM attrs for o1;
otherwise, update the data version in HSM attrs of o1 with the data version of o2.
if o2 has been archived, check whether whether the archive is dirty (HS_DIRTY).
if so, do nothing to the HSM attrs for o2;
otherwise, update the data version in HSM attrs of o2 with the data version of o1.
2. normal layout swap:

lfs swap_layouts o1 o2
As we don't know whether the content of o1 and o2 are same, thus on MDT:
if o1 has been archived, check whether whether the archive is dirty (HS_DIRTY).
if so, do nothing to the HSM attrs for o1;
otherwise, update the state with HS_DIRTY for HSM attrs of o1.
if o2 has been archived, check whether whether the archive is dirty (HS_DIRTY).
if so, do nothing to the HSM attrs for o2;
otherwise, update the state with HS_DIRTY for HSM attrs of o1.
3. data restore
MDT will swap the layouts after finished HSM data restore.
SWAP_LAYOUTS_MDS_HSM
do as it what does in Lustre currently.

All these modification must be in MDD layout in a transaction. Otherwise, it may result in an inconsistence.

--- Message (Ben Evans, 2019-12-04 14:44:10.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

(1 comment)

> >And it is not a normal case that the file is archived during
 > migration.
 > Should we probably prevent migration of archived file rather than
 > support it?

No, we should absolutely support it.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2019-12-04 15:35:12.000000000) ---
Patch Set 8:

> >And it is not a normal case that the file is archived during
 > migration.
 > Should we probably prevent migration of archived file rather than
 > support it?

I agree with Ben - allowing migration of a released file is useful. Doing OST migration of a released file is essentially a no-op, since there is no data to move. 

Doing MDT migration of the inode is more complex, since the FID is changed. This will need some extra work on the client/MDT to store the original FID in the inode. There is already a ticket open for this in Jira - LU-7607

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-12-04 06:23:14.000000000) ---
Patch Set 16:

> Probably, PTLDEBUG=all is not enough

Artem, it looks from the sanity-hsm logs that full debugging is enabled, but the debug_mb is too small to hold the full test logs:

 1638287092 == sanity-hsm test 607: release migrated archived file

 1638287099.896425 @@@@@@ FAIL: cannot release \/mnt\/lustre\/d607.sanity-hsm\/foodir\/f607.sanity-hsm 

but the main logs start at 1638287099.234418, so only hold about 0.65s with the full debug logs.  It makes sense to also increase the debug buffer size to capture enough of the log:

 Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity-hsm env=ONLY=607,PTLDEBUG=all,DEBUG_SIZE=128

and/or only enable "+info+hsm" instead of the all messages, so that more of the important messages fit into the buffer.
